# Crate Plan: mizar-checker

> Canonical language: English. Japanese companion:
> [../ja/00.crate_plan.md](../ja/00.crate_plan.md).

Status: autonomous crate-development plan. Preliminary task 0 created this
plan before [todo.md](./todo.md) task 1; task 1 has since added the crate
scaffold; task 2 has since added the `TypedAst` data-shape spec; task 3 has
since implemented the `typed_ast` data shapes; task 4 has since added the
`binding_env` spec; task 5 has since implemented the `binding_env` data layer
and module shell; task 6 has since added the `type_checker` spec; task 7 has
since implemented type-expression normalization; task 8 has since implemented
declaration and local-binding checking; task 9 has since implemented
term/formula inference over checker-owned payloads; task 10 has since
implemented coercion candidate and initial-obligation checking over
checker-owned payloads; task 11 has since implemented deterministic type-fact
queries over checker-owned fact tables and local contexts; task 12 has since
added the active `type_elaboration` corpus runner for the source-to-checker
payload extraction gap; task 13 has since added the
`registration_resolution` spec; task 14 has since implemented the
registration database data layer; task 15 has since added the
`cluster_trace` spec; task 16 has since implemented the cluster closure data
layer with trace recording; task 17 has since implemented cluster loop,
bound, and explicit contradiction failure handling; task 18 has since
implemented the reduction trace data layer over explicit payloads; task 19
has since implemented pending-registration validation and activation gating
over explicit payloads; task 20 has since implemented existential gates over
explicit payloads; task 21 has since added the `overload_resolution` spec;
task 22 has since implemented checker-local overload site/candidate
collection over explicit payloads; task 23 has since implemented
checker-local template expansion over explicit payloads; task 24 has since
implemented checker-local viability filtering over explicit recorded-evidence
payloads; task 25 has since implemented per-site specificity graph
construction over explicit comparison payloads; task 26 has since implemented
root selection, refinement joins, and inserted-view recording; task 27 has
since added the `resolved_typed_ast` spec; task 28 has since implemented final
resolved typed AST assembly; task 29 has since recorded deferred corpus
obligations; task 30 has since added a cross-module determinism suite; task 31
has since guarded public enum forward compatibility; task 32 has since added
the source/spec correspondence audit; task 33 has since added the bilingual
documentation sync audit; task 34 has since recorded the module-boundary
refactor gate audit; task 38 has since resolved the functorial-cluster `for`
applicability-guard decision; task 39 has since resolved property-implementation
coherence for overlapping mode domains; task 48 has since added the
syntax-free reserve source declaration producer seam; task 50 has since added
the same-module attributed reserve evidence-query bridge; task 51 has since
added the same-module local mode reserve expansion-gap bridge; task 52 has
since added the same-module local structure reserve evidence-gap bridge; task
53 has since added the attributed local structure reserve evidence-gap bridge;
task 54 has since added the attributed local mode reserve expansion-gap bridge;
task 55 has since added the bare local mode expansion bridge; task 56 has
since added the one-edge local mode expansion chain bridge; task 57 has since
added the local mode structure-RHS evidence-gap bridge; task 58 has since
added the local mode attributed-builtin RHS evidence-gap bridge; task 59 has
since added the attributed local mode reserve evidence-gap bridge; task 60 has
since added the attributed local mode structure-RHS evidence-gap bridge; task
61 has since added the attributed local mode attributed-builtin-RHS
evidence-gap bridge; task 62 has since added the local mode structure-RHS
chain evidence-gap bridge; task 63 has since added the local mode
attributed-builtin-RHS chain evidence-gap bridge; task 64 has since added the
attributed local mode bare-builtin chain evidence-gap bridge; task 65 has since
added the attributed local mode structure-RHS chain evidence-gap bridge; task
66 has since added the attributed local mode attributed-builtin-RHS chain
evidence-gap bridge; task 67 has since added the structure-qualified attribute
extraction-gap boundary; task 68 has since added the argument-bearing mode
reserve extraction-gap boundary; task 69 has since added the argument-bearing
structure reserve extraction-gap boundary; task 70 has since added the
bracket-form local mode reserve extraction-gap boundary; task 71 has since
added the bracket-form local structure reserve extraction-gap boundary; task
72 has since added the two-edge bare local-mode chain expansion pass slice,
task 73 has since promoted that same source-derived seam to three edges, task
74 has since replaced the temporary bare builtin-terminal chain-depth cap with
an AST-bounded structural source-derived rule, task 75 has since added the
source-derived local-mode forward-reference active-range boundary, task 76 has
since added the matching local-structure forward-reference active-range
boundary, task 77 has since added the matching local-attribute
forward-reference active-range boundary, task 78 has since added the imported
structure reserve-head extraction-gap boundary, task 79 has since added the
imported mode reserve-head extraction-gap boundary, task 80 has since added the
imported attribute reserve extraction-gap boundary, task 81 has since added the
argument-bearing local attribute reserve extraction-gap boundary and resolver
suffix projection, task 82 has since added the imported mode reserve provenance
bridge, task 83 has since added the imported structure reserve provenance
bridge, task 84 has since added the imported attribute reserve provenance
bridge for the documented `parser.type_fixtures::TypeCaseAttr` source case,
and the closeout task has since added this crate exit report.

## Responsibility

Owned behavior:

- implement pipeline phases 6-8: type checking, registration/cluster
  resolution, and overload resolution;
- consume `mizar_resolve::resolved_ast::ResolvedAst` plus
  `mizar_resolve::env::SymbolEnv` and produce `TypedAst`,
  `TypeFactTable`, `ResolutionTrace`, and `ResolvedTypedAst`;
- normalize soft type expressions into deterministic predicate-like forms;
- build layered checker-local typing contexts over resolver-owned symbol
  identities;
- infer term and formula types while preserving recoverable error state;
- record type facts, coercion candidates, and `InitialObligationId`-backed
  initial obligations without assigning `VcId`s;
- index pending and activated registrations, compute replayable cluster
  closure, apply reduction registrations with provenance, and detect bounded
  saturation failures;
- expand and filter overload candidates, select ordinary roots, join accepted
  same-root refinements, insert allowed `qua` views, and preserve failed sites;
- keep ids, debug renderings, diagnostics, fact queries, candidate order, trace
  order, and artifact-facing projections deterministic.

Out of scope:

- lexical, syntax, parser, frontend, module-index, source-loading, and package
  planning ownership;
- name lookup, import/export validation, label resolution, and signature
  collection, which remain owned by `mizar-resolve`;
- arbitrary first-order reasoning, ATP search, proof certificate acceptance,
  theorem validity checking, and kernel replay;
- `VcId` assignment, `ObligationAnchor` construction, VC generation, and proof
  policy decisions beyond emitting checker-local initial obligations;
- stable published artifact schemas, cache storage, LSP rendering, and build
  scheduling;
- activating unverified local registrations merely because they occur earlier
  in the same source pass.

Boundary rules:

- every checker fact must be explainable as a declared type predicate,
  checker-owned inference fact, or registration-derived fact with trace
  provenance;
- source behavior must follow `doc/spec/en/` and existing `.miz` test intent,
  not observed source convenience;
- recovered or erroneous nodes may receive partial typed output, but invalid
  facts must not be exported as verified metadata;
- active registrations used for automatic inference must come from accepted
  dependency artifacts or accepted local summaries; an interim policy may
  record pending/unverified registrations and generated obligations, but it
  must not make unverified registrations contribute automatic facts;
- no task may introduce proof search, hidden coercion insertion, unrecorded
  cluster facts, or return-type-based overload selection.

## Authority Order And Specification References

For language behavior, use the repository authority order:

1. `doc/spec/en/`
2. `tests/**/*.miz`
3. `tests/coverage/spec_trace.toml`
4. `tests/**/*.expect.toml`
5. `doc/design/`
6. `crates/`

Primary references:

| Ref | Requirement | Checker status |
|---|---|---|
| [architecture 01](../../architecture/en/01.ir_layers.md) | `TypedAst`, `ResolutionTrace`, and `ResolvedTypedAst` are immutable source-shaped IR layers. | Refined by tasks 2, 3, 15, 27, and 28. |
| [architecture 04](../../architecture/en/04.type_and_registration_resolution.md) | Phases 6-7 own type normalization, local type contexts, type facts, coercion candidates, registration databases, cluster closure, reduction provenance, and partial typing after diagnostics. | Primary design input for wave 1 and wave 2. |
| [architecture 05](../../architecture/en/05.overload_resolution.md) | Phase 8 owns template expansion, viability, specificity graphs, root selection, refinement joins, inserted views, failed-site preservation, and `ResolvedTypedAst`. | Primary design input for wave 3. |
| [architecture 16](../../architecture/en/16.substitution_and_binding.md) | Binding identity, alpha-equivalence, capture avoidance, and definition-time closures must remain deterministic. | Refined by task 4 and consumed by task 5. |
| [architecture 17](../../architecture/en/17.cluster_trace_format.md) | `ResolutionTrace` must explicitly record cluster and reduction steps with deterministic traversal and loop detection. | Refined by tasks 15-18. |
| [architecture 18](../../architecture/en/18.dependency_fingerprint.md) | Checker outputs contribute type, registration, cluster, reduction, overload, and inserted-view dependency slices. | Per-source contribution tracking is required in registration and overload tasks; cache storage is out of scope. |
| [architecture 19](../../architecture/en/19.failure_semantics.md) | Type errors, overload ambiguity, cluster loops, and blocked work need stable phase ownership and deterministic ordering. | Applies to all diagnostic-bearing tasks. |
| [internal 07](../../internal/en/07.crate_module_layout.md) | `mizar-checker` owns type checking, registration resolution, and overload resolution inputs. | Defines the module split used by `todo.md`. |
| [spec 03](../../../spec/en/03.type_system.md) | Soft types, radix types, attributes, and subtyping. | Consumed by tasks 6-11 and 20. |
| [spec 08](../../../spec/en/08.type_inference.md) | Inferred types, coercions, `qua`, and `reconsider`. | Consumed by tasks 6-11 and 21-28. |
| [spec 13](../../../spec/en/13.term_expression.md) | Term expressions, set expressions, choice terms, and term-level typing surfaces. | Consumed by tasks 6 and 9-11. |
| [spec 17](../../../spec/en/17.clusters_and_registrations.md) | Cluster, existential, functorial, and reduction registrations. | Consumed by tasks 13-20. |
| [spec 18](../../../spec/en/18.templates.md) | Template definitions and template argument behavior. | Consumed by tasks 21 and 23. |
| [spec 19](../../../spec/en/19.overload_resolution.md) | Ordinary overload root selection and active refinements. | Consumed by tasks 21-28. |
| [spec 22](../../../spec/en/22.error_handling_and_diagnostics.md) | Type, registration, overload, and diagnostic classes. | Stable public code ownership must be checked before user-facing diagnostics. |
| [mizar-test staged model](../../mizar-test/en/staged_model.md) | `type_elaboration`, `formula_statement`, and `advanced_semantics` stages order semantic corpus growth. | Task 12 creates the first checker stage runner; task 29 records deferred formula/advanced semantic obligations until runners and source payloads exist. |

## Relevant Existing Tests And Missing Coverage

| Test path | Current intent | Checker relevance |
|---|---|---|
| `tests/miz/pass/parser/pass_parser_type_expressions_001.miz` and matching fail cases | Parser accepts and recovers type-expression syntax. | Source syntax exists for task 7 normalization fixtures, but these are parse-only and do not test checker behavior. |
| `tests/miz/pass/parser/pass_parser_qua_terms_001.miz` and `fail_parser_qua_missing_type_001.miz` | Parser covers `qua` source shape. | Inputs for task 10 coercion candidates and task 26 view insertion; no checker assertions yet. |
| `tests/miz/pass/parser/pass_parser_consider_reconsider_001.miz` and matching fail case | Parser covers declaration and binding surfaces. | Inputs for tasks 5, 8, and 10; no checker assertions yet. |
| `tests/miz/pass/parser/pass_parser_registrations_001.miz` and matching fail case | Parser covers registration syntax and recovery. | Inputs for tasks 13-20; no active registration semantics yet. |
| `tests/miz/pass/parser/pass_parser_template_arguments_001.miz` and `pass_parser_template_references_001.miz` | Parser covers template argument/reference syntax. | Inputs for tasks 21 and 23; no overload-template semantics yet. |
| `tests/miz/pass/resolve/pass_resolve_declaration_symbol_smoke_001.miz` | Active declaration-symbol smoke coverage reaches resolver symbol collection. | Lower-stage prerequisite for checker tests that consume `SymbolEnv`. |
| `tests/miz/fail/resolve/fail_resolve_duplicate_theorem_symbol_001.miz` | Active resolver duplicate-symbol failure coverage. | Confirms some resolver failures occur before checker stages. |
| `tests/coverage/spec_trace.toml` planned/deferred `type_elaboration`, `formula_statement`, and `advanced_semantics` rows | Records future semantic obligations without active checker execution. | Task 12 adds the first active `type_elaboration` gap runner entry; task 16 adds active builtin type-expression pass coverage; task 29 records formula/advanced obligations as deferred rows without active fixtures. |
| `tests/miz/pass/types`, `tests/miz/fail/types`, `tests/miz/pass/attributes`, `tests/miz/pass/clusters`, `tests/miz/fail/clusters`, `tests/miz/fail/overload` | Directory placeholders. | `test_gap`: checker semantic fixture sets have not started. |

Planned test-first additions:

- task-local Rust unit tests for deterministic ids, tables, rendering, query
  APIs, trace ordering, candidate order, and diagnostic ordering;
- task 10 now adds Rust coverage for widening, source `qua`, and narrowing
  coercion candidates, sethood/non-emptiness/narrowing obligations, invalid
  `qua`, missing evidence, and non-consumable supporting facts;
- task 11 now adds Rust coverage for fact query provenance matching,
  deterministic canonical ordering, no fact duplication, local assumption
  visibility, missing context behavior, contradiction diagnostics, and
  non-mutating queries;
- task 12 now adds active `.miz` fail coverage for the missing
  source-to-checker type-elaboration payload bridge; task 16 adds active pass
  coverage only for source-derived builtin `set`/`object` type-expression
  normalization; Campaign II task 17 projects that supported slice through
  checker-owned `ResolvedTypedAst`; task 48 moves reserve binding/declaration
  handoff production into a checker-owned syntax-free seam; task 50 extracts
  same-module attributed builtin reserve payloads to the checker evidence-query
  diagnostic; task 51 extracts same-module local mode reserve heads to the
  checker missing mode-expansion diagnostic; task 52 extracts same-module
  local structure reserve heads to the checker missing evidence-query
  diagnostic; task 53 extracts attributed same-module local structure reserve
  heads to the checker missing evidence-query diagnostic; task 54 extracts
  attributed same-module local mode reserve heads to the checker missing
  mode-expansion diagnostic; task 55 extracts real AST-derived bare-builtin RHS
  expansions for same-module no-argument local mode reserve heads; task 56
  extends that pass slice by extracting one-edge same-module local mode chains
  whose dependency has an accepted bare builtin RHS expansion; task 57 extracts
  real same-module local-mode expansions whose RHS is a same-module local
  structure head to the checker evidence-query diagnostic for missing
  base-shape/constructor-witness evidence; task 58 extracts real same-module
  local-mode expansions whose RHS is an attributed builtin head to the checker
  evidence-query diagnostic for missing attributed-type existential evidence;
  task 59 extracts attributed same-module local mode reserve heads with real
  direct bare-builtin RHS expansions to the checker evidence-query diagnostic
  when the same mode is not mixed with a bare reserve use; task 60 extracts
  attributed same-module local mode reserve heads with real direct local
  structure RHS expansions to the checker evidence-query diagnostic when the
  same mode is not mixed with a bare reserve use; task 61 extracts attributed
  same-module local mode reserve heads with real direct attributed-builtin RHS
  expansions to the checker evidence-query diagnostic when the same mode is
  not mixed with a bare reserve use; task 62 extracts one-edge bare local-mode
  chains ending in a same-module local structure RHS to the checker
  evidence-query diagnostic for missing base-shape/constructor-witness
  evidence; task 63 extracts one-edge bare local-mode chains ending in an
  attributed builtin RHS to the checker evidence-query diagnostic for missing
  attributed-type existential evidence; task 64 extracts attributed same-module
  local mode reserve heads whose one-edge dependency chain ends in a bare
  builtin RHS to the same missing attributed-type evidence query; task 65
  extracts attributed same-module local mode reserve heads whose one-edge
  dependency chain ends in a same-module local structure RHS to the missing
  structure and attributed-type evidence query; task 66 extracts attributed
  same-module local mode reserve heads whose one-edge dependency chain ends in
  an attributed builtin RHS to the missing full attributed-type evidence
  query; task 67 keeps structure-qualified attribute references on the
  source-to-checker extraction gap until real qualifier and attribute-owner
  provenance exist; task 68 keeps argument-bearing same-module local mode
  reserve heads on the source-to-checker extraction gap until real
  type-argument and term-argument provenance exist; task 69 keeps
  argument-bearing same-module local structure reserve heads on the
  source-to-checker extraction gap until real type-argument and term-argument
  provenance exist; task 70 keeps bracket-form same-module local mode reserve
  heads on the source-to-checker extraction gap until real bracket
  type-argument and `qua`-argument provenance exist; task 71 keeps
  bracket-form same-module local structure reserve heads on the
  source-to-checker extraction gap until real bracket type-argument and
  `qua`-argument provenance exist.
  Imported,
  argument-bearing expansion, parameterized,
  contextual, ambiguous, or cyclic mode expansion,
  structure base-shape/full
  attributed-type existential evidence, and AST-wide task 7-11 payload
  extraction remain deferred without fabrication. Forward-reference acceptance
  is forbidden by active-range rules and covered only as a lower-stage
  rejection;
- task 14 now adds Rust coverage for pending registration non-firing,
  deterministic activation movement, per-source contribution round-tripping,
  invalid activation rejection, and stable checker-owned ordering/rendering;
- task 15 now specifies planned Rust coverage for trace-recorded cluster
  closure, loop/bound handling, reduction replay, strategy-audit diagnostics,
  and trace determinism; implementation coverage starts in tasks 16-18;
- task 16 now adds Rust coverage for replayable cluster closure, deterministic
  cluster step ordering, multi-antecedent conditional clusters, transitive
  chains, inactive/non-cluster non-firing, and mismatched activation payloads;
- task 17 now adds Rust coverage for direct and indirect cluster loops,
  depth and generated-fact bounds, zero-antecedent depth, explicit
  contradiction diagnostics, incomplete closure status, and cache-key-visible
  traversal settings;
- task 18 now adds Rust coverage for replayable reduction steps, architecture
  17 reduction provenance fields, inactive/rejected/non-reduction non-firing,
  invalid substitutions, missing guard evidence, strategy-audit mismatches, and
  `such` guards as applicability-only evidence;
- task 22 now adds Rust coverage for overload site coverage across supported
  roles, site and candidate provenance retention, source-written `qua`
  metadata retention, already-filtered candidate preservation, deterministic
  candidate order, duplicate site keys, missing candidate-site links, and
  deferred unsupported roles;
- task 23 now adds Rust coverage for explicit template expansion, omitted
  inference payloads, missing omitted inference, accepted/missing/deferred
  constraint evidence, source-`qua` widening/narrowing status, non-template
  priority, deferred unsupported candidates, exclusion diagnostics, and
  deterministic expansion rendering;
- task 24 now adds Rust coverage for exact matches, consumable fact widening,
  accepted source-`qua` coercions, pending/degraded/rejected/out-of-scope fact
  evidence, missing evidence, invalid narrowing, ambiguous inheritance,
  blocked/deferred external evidence, missing viability payloads, stable
  rejection/block diagnostics, and deterministic viability rendering;
- task 25 now adds Rust coverage for comparable, equivalent, and incomparable
  candidate pairs, accepted edge rendering, per-site graph construction,
  return-type-independent ordering, missing/duplicate/unknown/cross-site
  comparison payload diagnostics, and deterministic graph rendering;
- task 29 records deferred traceability entries for `formula_statement` and
  `advanced_semantics`; active `.miz` fixtures remain future work after those
  runners and the required source-to-checker payload seams land;
- task 38 adds inactive advanced-semantics coverage for the functorial-cluster
  `for` guard, pinning that consequents are unavailable outside the guarded
  result type until MC-G020/MC-G021/MC-G023/MC-G030 runner and payload gaps
  close;
- task 39 adds inactive advanced-semantics coverage for overlapping property
  implementations without a required coherence proof, deferred until
  MC-G020/MC-G030 runner and property-payload extraction gaps close;
- task 30 adds a checker-owned Rust determinism suite covering exact reruns
  and canonicalized equivalent-input permutations for type normalization,
  fact queries, cluster traces, overload candidate ordering/diagnostics, and
  final `ResolvedTypedAst` projection;
- task 31 records public enum forward-compatibility decisions in every checker
  module spec and adds a lint-policy guard that every plain `pub enum` remains
  `#[non_exhaustive]` and listed in the owning English/Japanese policy table;
- task 32 records a source/spec correspondence audit that inventories every
  current checker `pub mod` export, top-level public item, and public
  `dense_id!` / `string_key!` newtype, then traces promised behavior to source,
  Rust tests, or explicit gap/deferred rows; the lint-policy guard now checks
  that the audit covers the current public surface and MC-G rows;
- task 33 records a bilingual documentation sync audit covering every current
  English/Japanese checker design document pair, with `none` sync debt and a
  lint-policy guard over pair inventory and file pairing;
- task 34 records a module-boundary refactor gate audit over the current Rust
  source/test-support file layout, with no required behavior-neutral split and
  a lint-policy guard over the source layout inventory;
- the closeout task records `crate_exit_report.md` in English/Japanese,
  including task commits, hard gates, deferred items, verification, quality
  score, and next-crate handoff;
- no existing `.miz` tests or expectation sidecars may be rebaselined merely
  to match current source behavior.

  with a source-layout audit guard, without changing checker source behavior.
- The closeout task adds `doc/design/mizar-checker/en/crate_exit_report.md` and
  the Japanese companion without changing source behavior.
- Direct dependencies for the scaffold are `crates/mizar-session/` and
  `crates/mizar-resolve/`; later dependencies require task-scoped specs.
- Current resolver source surface includes `resolved_ast`, `env`, `symbols`,
  `labels`, `names`, and recovered-syntax handling. The checker must consume
  resolver-owned ids and opaque signature shells instead of redoing name
  lookup or symbol collection.
- Current corpus infrastructure has active parse-only and declaration-symbol
  runners. Task 12 adds an active `type_elaboration` runner that reaches
  frontend parsing and resolver symbol collection, then reports the missing
  checker payload-extraction bridge as an external dependency gap.

Observed behavior:

- `main` is exactly at local `origin/main` before task 0 (`51bcaed...`) with a
  clean worktree and no ahead/behind commits.
- `mizar-resolve` tasks 1-23 and 25-29 are complete; resolver task 24 was
  deferred at resolver close-out on the `mizar-artifact` `ModuleSummary`
  dependency.
- `mizar-artifact` now provides `ModuleSummary` and `RegistrationSummary`
  schemas, writers, and readers. Producer/reuse integration remains a later
  task for resolver and checker crates.
- `mizar-resolve` task 5 and task 20 are complete, so checker task 1's declared
  resolver prerequisites are available.
- `mizar-resolve` task 21 is marked complete, so later checker registration and
  overload tasks may inspect current signature-projection data, but each task
  must still verify whether the exact checker-needed payload exists before
  implementing behavior.

Observed behavior is inventory only. It is not normative unless supported by
`doc/spec/en`, tests, traceability metadata, design documents, or explicit
human approval.

## Known Gaps And Drift

The `Class` column records the protocol classification. User-requested
`external_dependency_gap` entries may appear directly when the missing input is
external to `mizar-checker`; when an already-classified item is also an
external-dependency or deferred planning gate, that status is recorded in the
evidence/action text.

`test_gap`, `source_drift`, and `design_drift`, not a `spec_gap`. Spec 4.3
already defines multi-name reserve segments and implicit theorem closure for
each free reserved identifier, Chapter 13 defines identifier terms, Chapter 14

generalizes only the runner-side payload bridge needed to preserve both binding
identities and the shared written type range. It leaves implicit
closure/order nodes, theorem acceptance, facts/truth, broader source shapes,
proof, CoreIr, ControlFlowIr, and VC deferred.

MC-G020 task 124 current-state override: this exact slice was classified as a
`test_gap`, `source_drift`, and `design_drift`, not a `spec_gap`. Spec 4.3
permits multiple top-level reserve directives and supplies examples with more
than one directive, while Chapters 13, 14, and 16 already define the identifier,
equality, and theorem surfaces. The real reserve producer already creates two
bindings with distinct written type ranges for two declarations, but the active
binary-formula extractor requires one `ReserveItem` and retains no explicit
pre-normalization result/expected inputs in its output. Task 124 promotes
only
`reserve x for set; reserve y for set; theorem MultipleReserveDeclarationEqualityPayloadBoundary: x = y;`,
generalizes the exact extractor to two reserve items for that config, and retains
operand-specific pre-normalization type inputs so both distinct source anchors
are reviewable. Semantic builtin `set` may still intern to one normalized type
with a canonical source representative; the task must not duplicate semantic

## Resolved Step 2 Spec Decisions

| ID | Class | Resolution |
|---|---|---|
| SSA-001 | `spec_gap` | Task 35 resolves constructor property arguments vs fields-only extensionality by adopting the fields-only constructor rule. Spec 05 and 07 now state that default constructors accept fields only, generate projection axioms only for fields, and leave property values to Chapter 7 property implementations. The inactive `advanced_semantics` seed `fail_structure_constructor_property_arg_001` and traceability rows `spec.en.05.structures.constructor_fields_only.semantic` / `spec.en.07.modes.property_implementation.not_constructor_source.semantic` pin the rejected constructor-property form until MC-G020/MC-G030 runner and payload gaps close. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-002, SSA-011, SSA-012 | `spec_gap` | Task 36 resolves structure member identity, implicit upcast path uniqueness, and inheritance acyclicity. Spec 05 now tracks inherited member identity as root declaration plus inheritance path/view, requires exact parent-member coverage and per-parent type-inclusion obligations discharged by the existing `coherence` block, preserves renamed same-root paths as distinct views, and names `structures.inherit.cycle` for cyclic inheritance. Spec 19 now states that implicit upcast uniqueness is syntactic over resolved `inherit` declaration paths. The inactive `advanced_semantics` seed `fail_structure_inherit_duplicate_member_coverage_001` pins duplicate parent-member coverage; existing structure/overload seeds remain valid, and the template view-leak seed guards cross-view evidence. No renamed-view reject seed was added because renamed-view exposure remains positive behavior. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-003, SSA-010, SSA-016, SSA-019 | `spec_gap` / editorial | Task 37 resolves overload tie-breaks, equivalent-root ambiguity, specificity preorder wording, and the duplicated §19.6.1 text. Spec 19 now compares instantiated concrete parameter vectors under the normal `⊑` preorder after template expansion; template declared constraint strictness is not a tie-breaker, non-template priority applies only to mutually equivalent concrete vectors, return type remains excluded, and ambiguity is a nonempty maximal-root set with more than one distinct ordinary root. Ordinary definitions with identical argument signatures are declaration conflicts regardless of return type. Architecture 05 and the checker overload design now match this rule. Inactive seeds `fail_overload_equivalent_roots_ambiguity_001`, `fail_overload_template_equivalent_roots_ambiguity_001`, and `fail_resolve_same_signature_same_return_conflict_001` pin ordinary/template-derived equivalent-root ambiguity and the same-return ordinary declaration-conflict rule; the last remains inactive until resolver declaration-symbol support grows beyond the current different-return diagnostic. Mizar-core task 26 / template-audit F7 records the separate Phase A omitted-template inference determinism rule. No checker/core/resolver source semantics changed. |
| SSA-004 | `spec_gap` | Task 38 resolves functorial-cluster `for` semantics. Spec 17 now treats the trailing `for` type expression as an applicability guard over the full known normalized result type, including parameters and attributes, and the coherence/FOL encoding includes that guard as a premise. Spec 16's proof-obligation summary and spec 23's registration-node discussion delegate the guarded functorial encoding to Chapter 17. The inactive seed `fail_cluster_functorial_for_guard_001` and traceability row `spec.en.17.clusters.functorial_for_guard.semantic` pin that a valid registration does not provide its consequent at same-radix use sites that lack the guarded attribute. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-005 | `spec_gap` | Task 39 resolves property-implementation coherence. Spec 07 now permits but conditionally requires a `coherence` block on property `means`/`equals` implementations when the implementation's normalized mode domain overlaps an earlier visible implementation of the same struct property; the obligation proves both implementations assign the same property value over the overlap. Spec 16 and Appendix A were synchronized. The inactive seed `fail_mode_property_overlap_missing_coherence_001` and traceability row `spec.en.07.modes.property_implementation.coherence.semantic` pin rejection of a narrower overlapping implementation without coherence, while deferred parser row `spec.en.07.modes.property_implementation.parser` records the property-implementation syntax support gap. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-006 | `design_drift` | Task 40 resolves registration activation timing. Spec 17 keeps item-ordered activation as the language contract and states that correctness acceptance may be asynchronous: implementation may keep modules/use sites pending while proof/artifact status is unresolved, but a completed verification pass must not finally reject later uses that become accepted after an earlier registration is accepted. Architecture 04 and `registration_resolution.md` now label task 19's no-accepted-input behavior as an interim conservative approximation to be lifted when `mizar-vc`/`mizar-proof`/artifact integration supplies accepted status. The existing inactive seed `fail_mode_existential_after_declaration_001` and traceability row `spec.en.17.clusters.registration_activation_timing.semantic` pin the negative non-retroactive slice; positive accepted-local activation remains deferred on MC-G020/MC-G021/MC-G025/MC-G026. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-007, SSA-008, SSA-020 | `spec_gap` | Task 41 resolves closure termination, contradiction detection, and `attr(args)`. Spec 17 now makes the restricted no-argument cluster `adjective` grammar a load-bearing termination premise, spec 19 points its closure fixpoint argument back to that premise, and architecture 04 treats saturation bounds as defensive failure diagnostics rather than successful truncated semantics. Spec 17.7.3 now maps contradictory derived attributes to closure-time fatal `cluster` diagnostics, including the static contradictory-consequent seed `fail_cluster_contradictory_consequent_001`. Spec 03/06/Appendix A define `attribute_name(args)` as a use-site positional application of a declared parameterized attribute while preserving the restricted cluster adjective grammar; active parser recovery for argument-bearing registration adjectives is traced by `spec.en.17.clusters.restricted_adjective_grammar.parser`. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-009 | `spec_gap` | Task 42 resolves reduction determinism. Spec 17 now defines normalization as a deterministic function of the term, in-scope activated reduction rules, and the discharged side-condition set available at the rewrite site. `such` side conditions are applicability-only guards backed by stable local-fact, trace, or citation evidence and are excluded from specificity. Rule selection is pattern-first, guard-second, with position-wise §19.2.3 guard comparison only after pattern comparison does not select a unique rule; remaining equal, mixed, or incomparable cases fall to the lexicographically smallest rule FQN. `registration_resolution.md` mirrors this rule. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-013, SSA-014 | `spec_gap` | Task 43 resolves parameterized sethood and built-in/base-shape inhabitation. Spec 07 now gives guarded mode-existence and sethood obligations over valid parameter tuples, makes exported sethood a module-interface semantic fact without exporting the concrete witness, and points mode RHS inhabitation to the 17.3.4 table. Spec 13 checks comprehension sethood at the resolved mode and normalized argument tuple. Spec 17 distinguishes attributed type expressions, which still require active existential registrations, from unattributed `object`, `set`, accepted mode applications, bare structure radixes, and bare schema type parameters inside template bodies. The bare-structure row is a constructor-witness rule over inhabited fields, excluding properties; the schema-parameter row is backed by the §18.10.2 schema-context assumption. Spec 18 template type actuals now use the same table. Existing inactive sethood/existential/template seeds keep their rejection intent; positive source-derived coverage remains deferred on runner and payload gaps. No checker/core source semantics changed. |
| SSA-015, SSA-017 | `spec_gap` / `test_expectation_drift` / `source_drift` | Task 44 resolves omitted `reconsider` justification and ambiguous omitted `coherence with` target inference. Spec 04/08/15/Appendix A now permit omitted `reconsider` simple-justification syntax, while spec 08/22 accept it only when proof-free widening, inheritance, cluster closure, or already recorded local type facts discharge every target-type obligation; otherwise `type.narrowing_requires_proof` requests an explicit proof. Spec 19/22 now reject omitted `coherence with` when several visible earlier roots of the same symbol kind and arity are strictly sharpened by the redefinition signature, using `resolve.ambiguous_redefinition_target` rather than declaration/import order or return type. Inactive seeds `fail_types_reconsider_omitted_justification_001` and `fail_overload_redefine_ambiguous_target_001` pin the negative cases; the existing parser omitted-justification rejection is recorded as deferred parser task 47. No checker/core source semantics changed. |

No checker semantic `source_undocumented_behavior` is observed through task 47:
the implemented `typed_ast`, `binding_env`, type-expression normalization,
declaration/local-binding checking, term/formula inference, coercion/
initial-obligation checking, type-fact query, and registration database data
layer, pending registration validation/activation gating, existential gates, cluster
closure/loop/bound trace sources, reduction trace source, and overload
site/candidate collection, template expansion, viability filtering, and
specificity graph construction, root selection, refinement join validation,
inserted-view recording, failed-site preservation, task-45 overload
tie-break/redefinition-target boundary regressions, task-46 fatal
contradiction and reduction side-condition trace identity regressions,
task-47 base-shape inhabitation evidence and omitted-`reconsider` gate
regressions, and
resolved typed AST assembly are covered by their English/Japanese design
documents, the task-32
source/spec audit, bilingual sync audit, module-boundary audit, crate exit
report, and task-local Rust tests. The task 12 runner and tasks 13, 15, 21, 27,
32, 33, 34, 45, 46, 47, and closeout documentation are documented without adding checker
semantic source behavior. Future source behavior without spec/test support must
be classified before it is kept, and it cannot remain at crate completion.

No blocking contradiction prevents crate closeout. The crate exit report records
the remaining deferred items and quality review outcome.

verified, and committed independently before the next task starts.

Task-specific forbidden behavior:

| Task | Forbidden behavior |
|---|---|
| 0 | Editing code, creating semantic stubs, or starting task 1 before the plan commit exists. |
| 1 | Adding checker semantics, fake typed outputs, or non-minimal APIs beyond the scaffold and guard. |
| 2 | Choosing implementation behavior not supported by architecture 04/01, or assigning `VcId`s. |
| 3 | Extending language semantics beyond `typed_ast.md`, or making arena ids proof/artifact identities. |
| 4 | Specifying resolver-owned lookup, proof obligations, or type inference behavior. |
| 5 | Re-implementing resolver symbol collection or inventing missing binding payloads. |
| 6 | Changing `doc/spec` semantics implicitly, or mixing implementation into a spec-only task. |
| 7 | Treating source spelling order, hash-map order, or current implementation quirks as normalization rules. |
| 8 | Accepting invalid bindings as verified facts or generating proof-search behavior. |
| 9 | Selecting ordinary overload roots, deriving new registration facts, or fabricating successful types after hard errors. |
| 10 | Assigning `VcId`s, discharging obligations, or treating narrowing as proof-free success. |
| 11 | Returning nondeterministic fact query order or duplicating semantically identical facts. |
| 12 | Rebaselining existing expectations to current checker output or activating cases without traceability. |
| 13 | Treating pending registrations as active or forking the architecture 04 registration boundary. |
| 14 | Inventing resolver registration payloads, artifact schemas, or activation status. |
| 15 | Forking the canonical architecture 17 trace schema or omitting replay fields. |
| 16 | Adding hidden cluster facts or relying on traversal accidents. |
| 17 | Silently truncating saturation, diverging, or making bounds invisible to configuration/cache keys. |
| 18 | Rewriting parser syntax, omitting guard evidence, or applying reductions without provenance. |
| 19 | Treating generated obligations as accepted proofs, activating unverified registrations, or bypassing the interim gating policy. |
| 20 | Exporting unverified inhabitants or using existential gaps as warnings only. |
| 21 | Using return types for ordinary root selection or making template behavior implementation-only. |
| 22 | Widening candidate sets by global `SymbolEnv` scans beyond resolver-filtered visibility. |
| 23 | Fabricating unsupported scheme/template source roles or using cluster expansion during template inference. |
| 24 | Deriving new facts, firing registrations, or performing new type inference during viability checks. |
| 25 | Building a global specificity DAG or relying on nondeterministic tie-breaking. |
| 26 | Using return-type tie-breakers, inserting narrowing views, or turning failed sites into valid output. |
| 27 | Adding implementation or omitting failed-site and metadata contracts from the spec. |
| 28 | Elaborating to core logic, dropping failed overload sites, or fabricating final definitions. |
| 29 | Adding advanced fixtures whose lower-stage prerequisites are not executable, unless explicitly deferred. |
| 30 | Making determinism tests depend on platform order, worker timing, or transient paths. |
| 31 | Leaving new public enums unclassified or undocumented in their owning specs. |
| 32 | Closing audit gaps without implementation/test evidence or explicit deferral. |
| 33 | Updating only one language companion without a documented sync reason. |
| 34 | Mixing behavior cleanup, API exposure, diagnostic changes, or schema changes into file moves. |

## Crate Completion And Exit Criteria

Hard gates:

- every non-deferred task in [todo.md](./todo.md) is committed independently,
  with one task per commit;
- no blocking/high specification inconsistency remains;
- no implemented source behavior remains that is absent from `doc/spec/en` and
  tests; behavior that cannot be specified/tested yet must be excluded from the
  milestone scope or left unimplemented as a deferred design item;
- milestone-owned specification items have `.miz` coverage, task-local Rust
  tests, or explicit deferred reasons;
- existing `.miz` tests and expectations were not changed merely to match
  implementation behavior;
- design docs, English/Japanese companions, and source remain synchronized;
- checker crate boundaries are not violated;
- required verification commands pass or have explicit unrun justification;
- read-only crate quality review assigns at least 90/100 after hard gates pass.

Verification commands:

```text
cargo fmt --check
cargo clippy -p mizar-checker --all-targets -- -D warnings
cargo test -p mizar-checker
cargo clippy --all-targets --all-features -- -D warnings
cargo test
```

Additional commands are required for resolver boundary, corpus, or shared
harness tasks as noted in [todo.md](./todo.md).

Crate exit report:

- added [crate_exit_report.md](./crate_exit_report.md) and the Japanese
  companion at crate closeout;
- includes task commits, review results, verification, deferred items, external
  dependency gaps, quality score, and next-crate handoff.

## Task 241 Exact Parenthesized Reserved-Variable Inequality Active Slice

Task 241 closes a `test_gap`, narrow `source_drift`, and `design_drift`, not a
`spec_gap`, for the exact `reserve x for set; theorem
ParenthesizedReservedVariableInequalityPayloadBoundary: (x) <> x;` source.
Task 223 supplies the real single-left `ParenthesizedTerm` producer and Task 121
the real reserve/`BindingEnv`/inequality consumer. The private shared
parenthesized binary-formula helper preserves the closed Task 223/233 wrappers
while the Task 241 config preserves independent wrapper/inner/right provenance,
ordinal 1/2 lookup to `BindingId(0)`, one canonical `BuiltinSet`, two inferred
terms, two ordered expected constraints, and one fact/candidate/diagnostic/
deferred-free checked inequality. Four shared backlinks plus one dedicated row,
the finite matrix, all 54 prior binary-formula owners bidirectionally, immutable
output, and a real sidecar protect active runner 183 within 398 cases / 362
requirements, type-elaboration 230/218, and pass/fail 214/184. Parenthesized
membership, imported or other parenthesized variants, desugaring/truth,
acceptance, proof/CoreIr/ControlFlowIr/VC, and downstream payloads receive no
Task 241 credit. Step 5 remains active; Steps 6/7 remain deferred. No checker
source/API/module-layout change was required.

## Task 242 Exact Parenthesized Builtin-Object Inequality Active Slice

Task 242 closes a `test_gap`, narrow `source_drift`, and `design_drift`, not a
`spec_gap`, for the exact `reserve x for object; theorem
ParenthesizedReservedObjectVariableInequalityPayloadBoundary: (x) <> x;` source.
Task 233 supplies the real object `ParenthesizedTerm` producer and Task 190 the
real object reserve/`BindingEnv`/inequality consumer. The closed Task 242 config
preserves independent wrapper/inner/right provenance, ordinal 1/2 lookup to
`BindingId(0)`, one written-`object`-anchored canonical `BuiltinObject`, two
inferred terms, six type entries, two ordered expected constraints, and one
fact/candidate/diagnostic/deferred-free checked inequality without object/set
coercion or an independent wrapper payload. Five shared backlinks plus one
dedicated row, the finite matrix, all 55 prior binary-formula owners
bidirectionally, focused Tasks 190/233/241 regressions, immutable output, and a
real sidecar protect active runner 184 within 399 cases / 363 requirements,
type-elaboration 231/219, and pass/fail 215/184. Parenthesized membership,
imported or other parenthesized variants, desugaring/truth, acceptance, and
downstream payloads receive no Task 242 credit; missing imported expansion/
evidence/signature payloads and proof/CoreIr/ControlFlowIr/VC remain deferred.
Step 5 remains active; Steps 6/7 remain deferred. No checker source/API/module-
layout change was required.

## Task 243 Exact Parenthesized Reserved-Variable Membership Active Slice

Task 243 closes a `test_gap`, narrow `source_drift`, and `design_drift`, not a
`spec_gap`, for the exact `reserve x for set; theorem
ParenthesizedReservedVariableMembershipPayloadBoundary: (x) in x;` source.
Task 223 supplies the real single-left `ParenthesizedTerm` producer and Task 120
the real reserve/`BindingEnv`/membership consumer. The unchanged Task 120
direct-right expected-set producer supplies the sole expected input. The closed
Task 243 config preserves independent wrapper/inner/right provenance, ordinal
1/2 lookup to `BindingId(0)`, one written-`set`-anchored canonical `BuiltinSet`,
two inferred terms, exactly five type entries, no left expected input, one
right-owned expected-set constraint, and one fact/candidate/diagnostic/deferred-
free checked membership without an independent wrapper payload. Four shared
backlinks plus one dedicated row, the finite matrix, all 56 prior binary-formula
owners bidirectionally, focused Tasks 120/223/233/241/242 regressions, immutable
output, and a real sidecar protect active runner 185 within 400 cases / 364
requirements, type-elaboration 232/220, and pass/fail 216/184. Only this exact
source now discharges the former parenthesized-membership extraction gap.
Object-left/set-right parenthesized membership and active imported provenance
remain outside Task 243 credit rather than globally deferred; missing imported
expansion/evidence/signature payloads and proof/CoreIr/ControlFlowIr/VC remain
deferred. Step 5 remains active; Steps 6/7 remain deferred. No checker source/
API/module-layout change was required.
